  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_26904996-adab-4476-95fc-aa3efe5d337a'

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer14117545475790711991">When Disney Imagineers installed hologram guides for the Magic Kingdom, using teenage models they had no idea the technology might backfire. But backfire it did: some nights when the kids go to sleep, they wake up in one of the Disney parks as a hologram.<br/><br/>With the adventures set forth in the first books now behind them, Kingdom Keepers 3: Disney In Shadow follows the five t</span>
  <span id="freeText14117545475790711991" style="display:none">When Disney Imagineers installed hologram guides for the Magic Kingdom, using teenage models they had no idea the technology might backfire. But backfire it did: some nights when the kids go to sleep, they wake up in one of the Disney parks as a hologram.<br /><br />With the adventures set forth in the first books now behind them, Kingdom Keepers 3: Disney In Shadow follows the five teens, Finn, Philby, Willa, Charlene, and Maybeck as they search to find Wayne, their mentor and head Imagineer who has mysteriously gone missing. Concerned Wayne has been abducted by the Overtakers—Disney villains, who along with other Disney characters, take over the parks when the turnstiles stop spinning, and want desperately to steer the parks to a far darker place—the five kids pick up a major clue from a close friend, Jez, whose dreams (nightmares, really) often accurately predict the future. <br /><br />The very few clues from Jez’s dream lead the kids into Disney’s Hollywood Studios and Epcot--through imaginary worlds that become real, by imaginary kids who are real. Each clue seems tied to the last, and with the stakes growing ever higher, what starts out as a puzzle ends up as a fight for their lives. Through a transparent paper box, a quest for a sword, rides on Soarin' and Maelstrom, life-and-death encounters with giant snakes, and a devious Maleficent, the Kingdom Keepers not only begin to decipher deeper meanings to the clues, but discover new truths about themselves and their ever-growing friendships.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14117545475790711991" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/112429345" />
    <a title="MissM" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/253444-missm"><img alt="MissM" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1499915366p2/253444.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/112429345?book_show_action=true">Jul 19, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="MissM" class="user" itemprop="url" name="MissM" href="/user/show/253444-missm">MissM</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/253444-missm?shelf=read-2010">read-2010</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer112429345" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14819425123239785687">For a series supposedly so heavily researched, they still get basic things wrong - and that's annoying.<br/><br/>Example? When you leave MK you have two options to get back to the Transportation and Ticket Center (TTC) - the ferry and the monorail. That's it. You can NOT take a bus from the gates of MK to the TTC. Buses go to the resorts from MK gates but NOT the TTC.<br/><br/>It's so aggravating that the little details continue to be wrong. Because it's in those little details that a true WDW fan who's reading the</span>
  <span id="freeText14819425123239785687" style="display:none">For a series supposedly so heavily researched, they still get basic things wrong - and that's annoying.<br /><br />Example? When you leave MK you have two options to get back to the Transportation and Ticket Center (TTC) - the ferry and the monorail. That's it. You can NOT take a bus from the gates of MK to the TTC. Buses go to the resorts from MK gates but NOT the TTC.<br /><br />It's so aggravating that the little details continue to be wrong. Because it's in those little details that a true WDW fan who's reading the series because it's about WDW, loses touch with the story.<br /><br />This book also was rife with revisionist history. Now apparently, Walt always planned to let the characters have free reign at nights, the CM's all know about it, the Overtakers don't want to take over the whole world, just the Parks, "Jez no, call me Jess" at the end of book one and back to Jez for book two is now firmly Jess again, "Sleeping Beauty Syndrome" turned to SBS is now just "The Syndrome," etc.<br /><br />And, again this book sets up for another so the story purposefully does not end.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14819425123239785687" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_167763769" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/167763769" />
    <a title="Drew Graham" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3346313-drew-graham"><img alt="Drew Graham" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1280704207p2/3346313.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/167763769?book_show_action=true">May 12, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Drew Graham" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Drew Graham" href="/user/show/3346313-drew-graham">Drew Graham</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3346313-drew-graham?shelf=me">me</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer167763769" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7952899910293252786">Yet again I thought maybe this book might just get it right, and yet again it didn't. The same problems from the first two apply here, except that this one is even longer and more drawn out, so it really seemed to drag and meander its way aimlessly through the flimsy plot. This time the DHIs take their adventure mostly to Epcot, making the selection for Overtakers pretty slim, so they included crash-test dummies from Test Track and random jesters from France in the World Showcase. Ultimately, af</span>
  <span id="freeText7952899910293252786" style="display:none">Yet again I thought maybe this book might just get it right, and yet again it didn't. The same problems from the first two apply here, except that this one is even longer and more drawn out, so it really seemed to drag and meander its way aimlessly through the flimsy plot. This time the DHIs take their adventure mostly to Epcot, making the selection for Overtakers pretty slim, so they included crash-test dummies from Test Track and random jesters from France in the World Showcase. Ultimately, after 500 pages of wandering here and there (with the occasional mix-up of <i>running</i> here and there), they ended up in a bizarre commandeering of Fantasmic, which ended up in a big mess that resolved itself in a matter of a few pages. With books like these (especially if they're so carelessly handled), you really can't put out more than 500 pages. The tiniest bit of editing could have streamlined at least 100.<br /><br />The writing is still pretty sad. The details and facts about the Disney Parks continue to be off (Dumbo is a girl? A character is named Wanda after "Mickey's wand"? And what wand would that be?), and the author continues to contradict his own history and mythology. There is an entire conversation at the start of this book that presumably took place during the first book, but which certainly did not, but which really should have, as it finally (tried to) explain how the whole system works and what the bad guys' motive is in the first place. References to previous events <i>in the same book</i> are inaccurate, and the rules here are so flimsy and malleable that nothing can be taken seriously. That doesn't mean, however, that the kids don't take it seriously. Oh no, everything is a crisis and everything is met with sarcasm and derision and snark. The characters have a <i>little</i> more personality, but they are still pretty wooden and one-dimensional, and there are way too many of them (in case five DHIs weren't enough, why don't we spend a good chunk of the plot watching amateur teenagers create complete DHIs of two of their more gifted friends?). One of the characters' first names still hasn't even been uttered. It was nice to see there wasn't any awkwardly-handled cursing in this one--it's almost like a very select few of the more obvious problems with each book, such as this one, are slightly rectified with the next one. Some of the text just doesn't make sense and could have very, very easily been fixed if only someone had bothered to proofread, which it isn't apparent that someone had. I mean, "uneven parallel bars"?? A few of the clueless parents are actually involved eventually, the baddies are somehow apprehended in the end, and a couple of mysteries are sort of solved, but by the time I was done wading through the plodding plot, I didn't really care that much. Oh, and I've never cared about obligatorily coot-ish Imagineer Wayne. It's not that hard not to care about him.<br /><br />These books are in desperate need of an editor and a fact-checker, both of which I can only assume they did not have. I have one more in hand, so I guess I'll just finish, and we'll see if it starts to make sense. The Disney Geek in me still somehow believes. This is definitely the weakest point in the series so far. We'll also see if these Overtakers actually start to resemble their film counterparts. At least I sort of understand their whole master plan now.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7952899910293252786" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText17594444771055100590" style="display:none">AWESOME!!!<br /><br />The Keepers, Finn, Willa, Maybeck, Philby, and Charlene are in for a ride! Alright, you see on the cover a kid hanging onto a snake. Yeah, sorry but I can't say what will happen. I can tell you about the teams. Overtakers: Villains who want to take over the parks. They want darkness and nightmares to have their run on the roller coasters. The Keepers: Five teens who are DHIs. During the night, when they sleep, they cross over into the parks and fight the Overtakers, keeping them at bay. They find out their plans, and stop them. The Fairlies: People who have cool powers. 'A curse' they call it.<br /><br /><br />The book had cool twists, turns, and excitement. There's more adventure and problems as the Keepers get further into the Overtakers plan.<br /><br />The ending is...Cool-O. I liked it, I loved it, you will to. No objections. Can't say more otherwise I'll spoil it.<br /><br /><br /><br /><br />I recommend this book to people who have read the previous books. People 9-Adult will love it, along with tweens, teens, and Disney lovers.</span>

But backfire it did: some nights when the kids go to sleep, they wake up in one of the Disney parks as holograms. <br/>The five teens have twice thwarted evil plots masterminded by Maleficent; but now Finn, Philby, Willa, Chalene, and Maybeck have another problem: Wayne, their mentor and head imagineer, has mysteriously gone missing. Concerned that Wayne has</span>
  <span id="freeText7818466641237261639" style="display:none">When Disney imagineers installed hologram guides for the Magic Kingdom using teenage models, they had no idea the the technology might backfire. But backfire it did: some nights when the kids go to sleep, they wake up in one of the Disney parks as holograms. <br />The five teens have twice thwarted evil plots masterminded by Maleficent; but now Finn, Philby, Willa, Chalene, and Maybeck have another problem: Wayne, their mentor and head imagineer, has mysteriously gone missing. Concerned that Wayne has been abducted by the Overtakers, the kids pick up a major clue from a close freind, Jess, whose dreams (nightmares, really) often accurately predict the future.<br />This time, the clues from Jess's dream lead the kids into Disneys Hollywood Studios and Epcot. Each clue seems tied to the last, and with the stakes growing ever higher, what starts out as a puzzle ends up as a fight for their lives. As they quest for a sword, take rides on Soarin' and Maelstrom, have life-and-death encounters with a giant snake, and attempt to stop Maleficent, the Kingdom Keepers not only begin to decipher deeper meanings in the clues, but discover new truths about themselves and theri ever-growing freindships. <br /><br />I really enjoyed this book thought it was amazing Ridley finds a way to keep you on your toes in points of this book, really loved it. if your a fan of Disney then you will truelly love this book. </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer15708393959201398328">Book 3 in the series...<br/><br/>"Kingdom Keepers 3: Disney In Shadow follows the five teens, Finn, Philby, Willa, Charlene, and Maybeck as they search to find Wayne, their mentor and head Imagineer who has mysteriously gone missing. Concerned Wayne has been abducted by the Overtakers—Disney villains, who along with other Disney characters, take over the parks when the turnstiles stop spinning, and want desperately to steer the parks to a far darker place—the five kids pick up a major clue from a close fr</span>
  <span id="freeText15708393959201398328" style="display:none">Book 3 in the series...<br /><br />"Kingdom Keepers 3: Disney In Shadow follows the five teens, Finn, Philby, Willa, Charlene, and Maybeck as they search to find Wayne, their mentor and head Imagineer who has mysteriously gone missing. Concerned Wayne has been abducted by the Overtakers—Disney villains, who along with other Disney characters, take over the parks when the turnstiles stop spinning, and want desperately to steer the parks to a far darker place—the five kids pick up a major clue from a close friend, Jez, whose dreams (nightmares, really) often accurately predict the future. The very few clues from Jez’s dream lead the kids into Disney’s Hollywood Studios and Epcot--through imaginary worlds that become real, by imaginary kids who are real. Each clue seems tied to the last, and with the stakes growing ever higher, what starts out as a puzzle ends up as a fight for their lives. Through a transparent paper box, a quest for a sword, rides on Soarin' and Maelstrom, life-and-death encounters with giant snakes, and a devious Maleficent, the Kingdom Keepers not only begin to decipher deeper meanings to the clues, but discover new truths about themselves and their ever-growing friendships."</span>

<div id="review_102981219" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/102981219" />
    <a title="Richard" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2116904-richard"><img alt="Richard" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1396829641p2/2116904.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/102981219?book_show_action=true">May 16, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Richard" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Richard" href="/user/show/2116904-richard">Richard</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer102981219" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17784893051746062280">The series has been going downhill since the first book. While I think the character interactions are still solid, the plotting was rather messy. The pacing between scenes and of the scenes themselves was a little wonky and disorienting; then, there was the fact that the logic and deductive skills feel much less clever than they did in the first book. The characters still seem astute, but the trail of clues in this installation was just a convoluted mess. Furthermore, Pearson continues to rely o</span>
  <span id="freeText17784893051746062280" style="display:none">The series has been going downhill since the first book. While I think the character interactions are still solid, the plotting was rather messy. The pacing between scenes and of the scenes themselves was a little wonky and disorienting; then, there was the fact that the logic and deductive skills feel much less clever than they did in the first book. The characters still seem astute, but the trail of clues in this installation was just a convoluted mess. Furthermore, Pearson continues to rely on the expectation that his reader base knows the park inside-out; and though certainly most of us are that sort of obsessive fan type, it's a weakness.<br /><br />Some of the concepts that are coming up are a little too over-the-top. I liked the simplicity of the concept in the first novel, which had a nice mix of magic and pseudo-science - but with Pearson adding hokey terminology and overthinking the process, it just weighs down the fun.<br /><br />I still think that he's doing somewhat poorly in keeping the characters consistent. Finn, Philby, Amanda, and Charlene are great. On the other hand, Maybeck seems way too gimmicky and though the idea of him being a token black character is lamp-shaded, I don't think Pearson realized how much of a flat character Maybeck is. Willa is completely opaque, simply by virtue of being invisible for so much of the series, even though she gets a bit of spotlight in the second book with the Syndrome stuff. They make her the wild card, but it's a thinly-veiled euphemism for "I don't know what the hell makes this character special, but I'm stuck with her." I almost thought she was going to betray the group, just so Pearson could get rid of this character that he hasn't really put much work into developing. Jess is a whole bucket of worms - though the biggest failure on that front is still the naming faux pas in the second book, where she retains the name that Maleficent gave her, rather than her real name.<br /><br />I'll keep reading the series, but I'm worried that Pearson is getting too sloppy in trying to be too ambitious with his plot.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17784893051746062280" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer4649276101217596381">Like the other Kingdom Keepers books, it's great entertainment! While I can't say it's high literature by any stretch of the imagination, it was very enjoyable. At times the plot seemed to twist a little TOO much, making it a bit convoluted for the light reading.   <span id="freeText4649276101217596381" style="display:none">Like the other Kingdom Keepers books, it's great entertainment! While I can't say it's high literature by any stretch of the imagination, it was very enjoyable. At times the plot seemed to twist a little TOO much, making it a bit convoluted for the light reading. But the action was good, and I liked that it was fast-paced. If I have one big complaint (and I say this as a Walt Disney World Cast Member who is very well acquainted with the parks), it's the lack of accuracy in some of the park information. Obviously some of it is creative license, done to move the plot along, but some things really could have used the editing eye of someone more familiar with the parks. As a simple example, the use of "Disney" Hollywood Studios instead of its proper name, Disney's Hollywood Studios. But that being said, you can't go wrong when you actually put Wonders of Life to use - 'cause Disney sure ain't! ;)</span>

<div id="review_215444347" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/215444347" />
    <a title="Aaron" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1196851-aaron"><img alt="Aaron" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1472240281p2/1196851.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/215444347?book_show_action=true">Sep 26, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aaron" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aaron" href="/user/show/1196851-aaron">Aaron</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer215444347" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10586449691201398175">Finn Whitman along with his friends Philby, Willa, Charlene, and Maybeck, who were hired to model Disney Host Interactive hologram guides for the parks at Disney World are back for another adventure in which they take on the Overtakers, who are led by Maleficent and Chernagog (the demon from Fantasia. The Overtakers are hoping to conquer the world, which is not surprising because they are made up of all the worst villains from the Disney films.<br/><br/>This time the DHIs are having to deal with the loss </span>
  <span id="freeText10586449691201398175" style="display:none">Finn Whitman along with his friends Philby, Willa, Charlene, and Maybeck, who were hired to model Disney Host Interactive hologram guides for the parks at Disney World are back for another adventure in which they take on the Overtakers, who are led by Maleficent and Chernagog (the demon from Fantasia. The Overtakers are hoping to conquer the world, which is not surprising because they are made up of all the worst villains from the Disney films.<br /><br />This time the DHIs are having to deal with the loss of their wise leader, the Imagineer Wayne. He has mysteriously gone missing, and it will be up to Finn and the gang to save him. They will have some extra help in the form of Jess and Amanda, two girls in foster care with their own special talents. Jess can see the future in her dreams. They will join the rest of the Kingdom Keepers and Wayne's daughter Charlene in the hopes of finding Wayne before the Overtakers' evil plot come to fruition.<br /><br />The previous books in the series focused on the Magic Kingdom and Animal Kingdom, but the focus in this tale shifts to Epcot and MGM Studios, and it is going to take every skill and teamwork for the Kingdom Keepers to prevent the Overtakers plans.<br /><br />As a big fan of all things Disney, I have really been enjoying this series, though, it took me forever to get to this volume, which originally came out in 2010. I do have to say that I thought it dragged a bit. There was a lot of setup (about 200 pages before things really got going) and a lot of talking about what the kids were going to do before anything really started to happen.<br /><br />It is interesting watching the Kingdom Keepers as they, and their relationships, evolve and developed, which is part of why the book is as thick as it is. I did miss having a lot of interaction with the Overtakers, which seemed to be the part that was missing the most in this volume.<br /><br />Finn, and the rest of the kids' parents, are definitely starting to notice things ... you probably would if your kid kept shifting into a hologram on a regular basis when falling asleep. This becomes a major problem when the kids end up trapped for a while, leaving their human bodies in something like a coma.<br /><br />I am definitely looking forward to Volume IV, which is also already out. I am hoping that the writing will be a little tighter and the book not quite as long.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10586449691201398175" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_3646587857" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3646587857" />
    <a title="Kiana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/36504237-kiana"><img alt="Kiana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1567452711p2/36504237.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3646587857?book_show_action=true">Nov 15, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kiana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kiana" href="/user/show/36504237-kiana">Kiana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781368046275" href="/book/show/51300501-kingdom-keepers-iii">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36504237-kiana?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36504237-kiana?shelf=disney-publishing">disney-publishing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36504237-kiana?shelf=bad">bad</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36504237-kiana?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3646587857" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10211753955152527120"><b>
  <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1094737601?book_show_action=false' rel='nofollow noopener'>My review of the original <i>Disney in Shadow</i>.</a>
</b><br/><br/>Of the three republished <i>Kingdom Keepers</i> books, <i>Disney in Shadow</i> is far and away the best of the three. It’s still not a <i>good</i> book, but it’s the only one that bothered to substantially alter any of the content, whereas the first book just fixed some typos and the second technically rewrote a lot of sentences but changed none of the substance. <br/><br/>The most admirable part of the 2020 <i>Disney in Shadow</i> is that it had the decency to write original material t</span>
  <span id="freeText10211753955152527120" style="display:none"><b>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1094737601?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">My review of the original <i>Disney in Shadow</i>.</a>
</b><br /><br />Of the three republished <i>Kingdom Keepers</i> books, <i>Disney in Shadow</i> is far and away the best of the three. It’s still not a <i>good</i> book, but it’s the only one that bothered to substantially alter any of the content, whereas the first book just fixed some typos and the second technically rewrote a lot of sentences but changed none of the substance. <br /><br />The most admirable part of the 2020 <i>Disney in Shadow</i> is that it had the decency to write original material to showcase the new attractions and ideas. I haven’t forgotten the lame “pick a thing out of a tree in Pandora instead of a generic recycling bin” stunt of <i>Disney at Dawn</i>, but this book doesn’t painfully attempt to make previous text accommodate new material - rather, it scraps a good 50% of the existing text and added a great deal of new stuff. And it doesn’t even feel like it’s going through the motions: the new sequences on the Ratatouille ride and in the various Pavilions are genuinely creative and inspired, not to mention a whole lot better than the tepid Epcot adventures that they replaced. (The one exception might be the loss of the Maelstrom chapter, but that’s not a loss I’m horribly sad about.) <br /><br />It’s also just much less of a slog than the original release. I noted in my review of <i>Disney in Shadow</i> that the third book suffers from a whole lot of bloated (and wholly unnecessary) filler, and the rewrite is the opposite of that. I’d wager that the new <i>Disney in Shadow</i> is half the length of the 2010 publication, and maybe even less than that. Some of this comes from the omission of a lot of the original’s pointless scenes, and some of it comes from trimming down a bunch of the paragraphs and establishing details. It wastes far less time twirling in circles and contemplating how to do things and instead just <i>does</i> them.<br /><br />At times, this zippiness is a little disheartening; the original release was sludgy, but this <i>Disney in Shadow</i> feels arguably more tired at times, like it didn’t want to re-experience the story any more than I did as a reader. There’s a definite “keep it moving” attitude at play, and it’s hard to say if that was a deliberate stylistic choice to appeal to less patient readers or just the rewrite being super bored with the original publication. <br /><br />The manic storytelling certainly reads as more childish than the original (and it kills whatever halfway good subtle character moments Pearson pulled off in the first release), but there’s no denying that it’s a much more palatable experience. If the first <i>Disney in Shadow</i> felt like wading through molasses, the rewrite feels like it’s on amphetamines. It’s still a somewhat unpleasant and embarrassingly amateurish read, but if you had me at swordpoint and demanded that I sit through one of them again, I wouldn’t hesitate to pick the 2020 version. It’s swifter, more focused, and over in a mercifully short period. <br /><br />Of course, the lack of proofreading and polish in the rewrite is as atrocious as the original, if not a little more so. Despite all of the new chapters being no more than 3 pages each, there are still multiple inconsistencies in which characters are where and doing what. An example: when Amanda and Willa infiltrate the Ratatouille ride, a line of dialogue is attributed to Charlene, even though Charlene isn’t with them. Another example: in England, “Jess read Willa’s lips,” even though it’s Jess and Charlene in the England sequence, and Willa’s over in France with Amanda. Even in the second publication, no one could be bothered to keep proper track of the characters for more than a minute. <br /><br />The new dialogue is also terrible. The <i>Kingdom Keepers</i> books have always had horrible conversations and one-liners, particularly among the teenagers, so that’s just staying the course, but I have to say that my least favorite bit actually went to Maleficent this time around. During the Fantasmic! confrontation with Finn, which should be epic and gripping, she says, “I’m a movie star now. I get what I want.” Has Pearson ever been able to write a Maleficent that even vaguely resembled the Disney character? No. But if you can stomach the image of a Fantasmic! Maleficent in the book’s climax saying this to her enemy and find it at all effective or threatening, then the <i>Kingdom Keepers</i> series might just be for you. <br /><br />Anyway, those are my overall thoughts on the updated <i>Disney in Shadow</i>. The best of the three by far - but given what we've been working with, take that with a grain of salt. <br /><br />A more detailed breakdown of the changes in the new edition (for people who don’t want to read the two versions for themselves) is below: <br /><br />* Jess’s initial vision of Wayne is different - it’s of seaweed (being in the Nemo lounge) in the background rather than the Wonders of Life, and there’s no anagram at all (and good riddance to that).<br /><br />* A lot of establishing details are removed. For instance: the scene of Finn and Philby encountering a security guard while entering Hollywood Studios and having to pretend to be their DHIs is cut. When the Keepers reach the soundstage building, Pearson omits the part where Finn and Maybeck enter first and scope out the space, and instead just has all five characters walk in. The characters also don’t have to dress up as <i>High School Musical</i> characters to get through Hollywood Studios unnoticed; they just show up. <br /><br />* To get Amanda and Jess onto the recording soundstage, Wanda tells Mrs. Nash that she’s taking them on a school tour instead of the previous edition’s complicated scheme with Mrs. Nash being at Mass and Maybeck distracting all of the other girls with a night at his aunt’s pottery shop. <br /><br />* Finn is no longer the only special Keeper who can enter the all-clear state and has to accompany every other Keeper in order to walk through doors and unlock them from the inside. Now, all of the Keepers can just do it, which streamlines a lot of the sequences. <br /><br />* The whole issue-but-not-really-an-issue-because-it-was-never-resolved of Finn not being able to enter or leave his all-clear state at will is totally gone. <br /><br />* The chapter of Finn and Philby in the Hollywood Studios control room is reduced to a couple of pages, and there is no struggle of them trying to leave without being caught by the guards.<br /><br />* A lot of pointless scenes between Finn and his mom, most of which just consisted of him resenting her for trying to connect with him, are cut. <br /><br />* Literally 84 pages are straight-up gone, from Finn and Philby infiltrating the Base at Hollywood Studios and gathering data to the characters decoding the anagram and watching <i>Dumbo</i> and infiltrating Epcot and Wonders of Life and being chased by Gigabyte. <br /><br />* There is a new scene where the Keepers go to the VIP lounge at the Living Seas. This is where they solve the box from Wayne, not in the back rooms of Crazy Glaze (as they did in the first version).<br /><br />* At least 200 pages, if not more, in the middle of the book are completely scrapped and rewritten (and are now way shorter). Instead of splitting up between France and Norway and Mission: Space and Soarin’, the characters just decide to search all of the Epcot pavilions. Willa and Amanda search Canada (where they get attacked by a flying totem) and then France, where they go on the Ratatouille ride looking for a sword (because a sword is apparently the equivalent of a really big knife). Skinner and Mabel (who are huge, because the ride is from the perspective of the rats) come to life, as well as some shadow snakes, and Mabel literally fires a giant shotgun at the characters. This sequence is actually terrifying in concept, so I liked it. <br /><br />* Charlene and Jess search in England, where they sneak into the Sportsman’s Shoppe, find a sword, and are locked in by a curse with a bunch of blaring clocks. Also a rather cool idea, even if it was technically a narrative dead end. <br /><br />* Maybeck and Philby go to Stave Church in Norway instead of the Maelstrom ride. They take Odin’s sword and are attacked by statues of Odin, Freya, Loki, and Thor that come to life. They also get the allegiance of a plaster Norwegian warrior, and that’s pretty great.<br /><br />* Finn goes to the Mexican plaza, and skulls and skeletons come to life and whack him with canes. <br /><br />* There’s a really awkward new scene where Willa tells Amanda that Charlene also likes Finn but that Amanda shouldn’t worry about it because Finn totally likes her more, and Amanda brushes it aside saying that she has bigger issues than a boyfriend. <br /><br />* There is no subplot about losing the fob and all of the Keepers being trapped in Sleeping Beauty Syndrome for the second half of the book. <br /><br />* There is also no cryptic message from Wayne about one of the Keepers being a traitor. <br /><br />* Everything about the “flight” subplot (Soarin’, Mission Space, Test Track) is cut, as is the Keepers’ failed attempt to rescue Wayne and escape from Wonders of Life. <br /><br />* In this version, Finn’s mom gets mad about him crossing over and demands that if he rescues Wayne at Fantasmic!, he and the other Keepers must do it in human form instead of as holograms. This leads to all of the Keepers having to sneak off and go to sleep in weird locations like their school wrestling rooms instead of their homes because they don’t want to be caught by their parents. It’s quite stupid, and I’m not sure why it was added. Also, Finn’s argument with his mom contains the unnecessarily harsh line, “I’ve met real monsters. And you’re worse than that.” Okay, Pearson, I get that Finn’s a teenager and teenagers can be mean to their parents, but that’s a bit much. <br /><br />* The characters still infiltrate a Fantasmic! dress rehearsal rather than an actual performance, but this dress rehearsal is about an hour before the show, as opposed to in the original version where it was at 5 a.m. (in other words, before the park opened to the public), which doesn’t seem right given that guests would be in the park at this time.<br /><br />* Also, Finn now fights Maleficent in the full Mickey costume rather than just as himself. React to that how you will. <br /><br />* Finn and Philby’s moms break into Epcot by apparently hopping a back fence. This is a totally plausible scenario, given the extent of Disney security in the theme parks. I’m sure any random mom could totally infiltrate Epcot like it’s a local baseball field. <br /><br />* Even better, once the moms are in Epcot, they proceed to burst into the closed Fantasmic! amphitheater, taking things to a whole new level of “how???” I can accept the Keepers getting in because they’re holograms and sneaking around the parks is their job, but actual inexperienced humans? Nope. (It’s also utterly pointless because the moms don’t end up doing anything or contributing in any way; they might as well have stayed home.) <br /><br />* Instead of being imprisoned on an Epcot barge, Wayne is trapped in Fantasmic!'s Steamboat Willie. Finn and Charlene go to rescue him and are attacked by... Titans? Pearson refers to the Titans as “Hades’s servant,” which I don’t think is right because Hades is an Olympian, and I can’t recall Hades ever having the Titans on his side in any version of the mythology. Whatever. Hades also shows up, and the Keepers fight him.<br /><br />* As Finn and Charlene rescue Wayne, Maybeck, Amanda, Philby, and Willa fight the legion of loa, or Dr. Facilier’s “friends on the other side.” And somehow all it takes to defeat them is to physically trip the spirits with a cable and plunge them into the water? Even though they’re spirits and therefore incorporeal? I don’t know. <br /><br />* There’s also a new chapter at the end that is utterly pointless except that it name-drops Galaxy’s Edge and says that the Keepers rode all the Galaxy's Edge rides a bunch of times because they had the parks to themselves. Then, right after this plug, the Keepers all reiterate that something is off about the parks and that they need to keep fighting, which I found somewhat hilarious, because one would think that if the parks felt off, they wouldn’t just be whooping it up on the rides - especially when rides are known to attack them and the parks are constantly surveilled by the Overtakers. Oh, <i>Kingdom Keepers</i>, logic is not thy strong suit.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10211753955152527120" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_292061323" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/292061323" />
    <a title="Kathy Davie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4222001-kathy-davie"><img alt="Kathy Davie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1285089902p2/4222001.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/292061323?book_show_action=true">Mar 10, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kathy Davie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kathy Davie" href="/user/show/4222001-kathy-davie">Kathy Davie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4222001-kathy-davie?shelf=children">children</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4222001-kathy-davie?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer292061323" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16151310362324166470">Third in the Kingdom Keepers fantasy adventure series revolving around a group of middle-schoolers charged with preventing the Overtakers from taking over Disney World.<br/><br/><br/><b>My Take</b><br/>I don't know if I'm getting used to the story or if Pearson is easing up… <br/><br/>The story is about an initial group of five kids, the Keepers, who play detective in the Magic Kingdom foiling the plots of the Overtakers. There is something in the hologram code that allows the kids to dream their way over to Disney World and into t</span>
  <span id="freeText16151310362324166470" style="display:none">Third in the Kingdom Keepers fantasy adventure series revolving around a group of middle-schoolers charged with preventing the Overtakers from taking over Disney World.<br /><br /><br /><b>My Take</b><br />I don't know if I'm getting used to the story or if Pearson is easing up… <br /><br />The story is about an initial group of five kids, the Keepers, who play detective in the Magic Kingdom foiling the plots of the Overtakers. There is something in the hologram code that allows the kids to dream their way over to Disney World and into their holographic counterparts. The kids have the usual issues with school and their parents although the whole running around in hologram bodies while their physical bodies are asleep is a bit different from the usual. Even as they have terrific adventures on various rides in the Kingdom.<br /><br />And it's not just the Overtakers the Keepers have to avoid. According to their DHI contracts, they're not allowed to walk into the park any ol' time. And getting caught could void their contracts and stop the flow of all the college money! They also have to get out of the park before day breaks or suffer Sleeping Beauty Syndrome!<br /><br />Interesting little talk Philby has with Maybeck about the chip on his shoulder. Philby makes a good point.<br /><br />I do like the challenges Pearson comes up with for the kids. Uh-ohhhh, Finn's mom, the NASA scientist, gets <em>really</em> suspicious! Poor Philby! Getting ready to dream one night, he gets caught out in his underwear!!<br /><br />For the film-geeks, Pearson includes information on how Disney coordinates Soarin' and the big show that is the denouement for the story.<br /><br /><br /><b>The Story</b><br />Finn and the gang are desperate to find Wayne. The Overtakers have kidnapped him and the kids desperately need him back. For himself. For the knowledge he has of the Kingdom.<br /><br /><br /><b>The Characters</b><br /><strong>Wayne Kresky</strong> is the old Imagineer who started them on their original adventures, but the Overtakers have kidnapped him. <br /><br /><strong>Finn Whitman</strong> is turning into a natural leader for the Kingdom Keepers with increasingly better control of turning himself into light. <strong>Charlene Turner</strong> is the "clean cheerleader" type with uncanny physical ability who has finally found her niche in the group. <strong>Isabella "Willa" Angelo</strong>. <strong>Dill Philby</strong> is the geeky sports enthusiast with a major talent for computers and he, Maybeck, and Jess finally manage to do Whitman's light trick---in the nick of time. <strong>Terry Maybeck</strong> is the oldest of the group and is starting to consider others. <br /><br /><strong>Amanda Lockhart</strong> and <strong>Jezebel "Jess"</strong> are Fairlies, something more than human. Amanda has some magical ability while Jess dreams the future. After their last adventure, their refuge was discovered and now they're in fostercare with <strong>Mrs. Nash</strong>. Finn and company need their help and Philby is determined to film them and create DHIs of Amanda and Jez. <strong>Wanda Alcott</strong> is actually Wayne's daughter and plays a very useful part in this installment. I'm hoping she or one of the other parents will help out with Amanda and Jess.<br /><br /><strong>Aunt Bess "Jelly" Maybeck</strong> is Terry's aunt with whom he lives. <strong>Gladis Philby</strong> is Philby's very worried mother. <strong>Maleficent</strong>, the nasty witch from <em>Sleeping Beauty</em> is the chief villainess and she's fronting for an even bigger villain, <strong>Chernabog</strong>.<br /><br /><strong>Greg "Lousy" Luowski</strong>, a fellow student at their school, has a thing for Amanda, but bullies everyone. His "pilot fish" friends are <strong>Mike Horton</strong> and <strong>Eric Kreuter</strong>.<br /><br /><br /><b>The Cover</b><br />I do love these hologram covers! In this one, Finn is flying through the air hanging onto the snake's tail while Spaceship Earth does a good job of imitating that holographic effect. Charlie and Willa are running to yet another disaster.<br /><br />The title set-up drives me nuts. Again. The series name with its number are huge while the actual title of this book about five times smaller...almost a nonentity.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16151310362324166470" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

      <span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_review_292061323'><a id="like_count_review_292061323" rel="nofollow" href="/rating/voters/292061323?resource_type=Review"><span class="likesCount">1 like</span></a>&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it gr-button gr-button--small" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F6275997-disney-in-shadow">Like</a></span>

<div id="review_430109979" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/430109979" />
    <a title="Chris" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1124585-chris"><img alt="Chris" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1209425909p2/1124585.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/430109979?book_show_action=true">Oct 08, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chris" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chris" href="/user/show/1124585-chris">Chris</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1124585-chris?shelf=i-own">i-own</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer430109979" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6430342509986857193">Disney in Shadow is Book 3 in the Kingdom Keeper Series. While this book does provide segments of back story as needed there are many elements that seem to rely at least somewhat on familiarity with the previous books. So if you haven't read those, you should probably do so before jumping in here. That said, the storyline does stand on its own without relying heavily on the history from the previous two books.<br/><br/>The DHIs know that trouble is brewing. At the end of book 2, the DHIs have saved Jez bu</span>
  <span id="freeText6430342509986857193" style="display:none">Disney in Shadow is Book 3 in the Kingdom Keeper Series. While this book does provide segments of back story as needed there are many elements that seem to rely at least somewhat on familiarity with the previous books. So if you haven't read those, you should probably do so before jumping in here. That said, the storyline does stand on its own without relying heavily on the history from the previous two books.<br /><br />The DHIs know that trouble is brewing. At the end of book 2, the DHIs have saved Jez but were unable to prevent the escape of Maleficent and Chernabog. Worse still (or maybe just as bad), Wayne has vanished. During the second book, Wayne was in hiding and only communicating with the kids through secure and cryptic messages. At the end of the book it is apparent that the Overtakers have captured Wayne.<br /><br />Knowing that Wayne is the only person who has the knowledge to adequately guide the kids, Finn desperately leads the DHIs in an effort to find him. From his experience inside the Disney computer system in book 2, Philby is able to hack into the DHI system and help control when and where the kids materialize after dark. This is helpful but there is still too much ground to cover. Amanda and Jess get more fleshed out as characters and we learn more about their special powers. Unfortunately they are also being threatened with a return to a "foster care" facility that would take them out of the state and thus unable to help. Crunched for time, the kids come up with a plan to make Amanda and Jess into DHIs as well. They area also introduced to a woman claiming to be Wayne's daughter. There is a lot of distrust at first but she proves very helpful later on.<br /><br />Even though the kids search for Wayne in all of the different parks, most of the action in this book takes place in Disney Studios and in Epcot. Jess has dreams and premonitions that she records in a diary. Wayne seems to have some idea of what Jess might see and so he's able to send clues to her through her diary messages. Wayne's sister also provides a cryptic clue for the kids to follow. One of Wayne's messages also seems to suggest a potential traitor in the group which puts everybody on edge. <br /><br />During their search, the DHIs once again have to watch out for the normal Disney security and maintenance teams as well as a growing supply of Overtakers. There are some pretty exciting sequences where the kids are battling with or fleeing from the various Overtaker minions. Even though the kids still do some very extraordinary things against extraordinary odds, this book seemed more realistic in terms of the kids actually being in mortal danger.<br /><br />The climax of the story takes place during a rehearsal for Fantasmic (one of my favorite Disney Parks shows). The scene does a great job of ratcheting up the tension as well as making any success come at great cost and loss.<br /><br />So far this is my favorite of the Kingdom Keeper books, mainly because it is increasing in complexity and intensity. The characters are still a little cheesy, but they seem to be growing more relatable. The situations are crazy of course but there is just enough realism to keep the suspense going. Probably my biggest complaint at this point is that I want the kids to have more allies…or any allies really. Specifically I would love to see some of the "good" Disney characters show up to start helping the DHIs. After all, the Overtakers have amassed quite the little army. It only seems fair that the DHIs should have some Disney heroes on their side. At the same time, that might make things either too unbalanced or too over-the-top.<br /><br />All in all, this is another fun addition to a fun series. It's not "high literature" by any means and it's definitely geared towards kids…but for a Disney fan like me, it's a lot of fun and I'm ready for the next adventure.<br /><br />***<br />3 out of 5 stars (for adult readers)<br /><br />****<br />4 out of 5 stars (for child readers)<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6430342509986857193" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1296897307" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1296897307" />
    <a title="Noah" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/35120920-noah"><img alt="Noah" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1296897307?book_show_action=true">Jun 02, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Noah" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Noah" href="/user/show/35120920-noah">Noah</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1296897307" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14722987122231394774"> A Review of Kingdom Keepers 3 by Ridley Pearson <br/> Being a Disney Host is glorious. You get to be a hologram guiding people around the Disney Parks. But Finn and his friends aren't just holograms that guide people around. At night, when they go to sleep, they wake up in Disney World as DHI's (holograms) and they fight evil to keep Disney safe. The "evil" is called the Overtakers, and they are trying to make Disney World a nightmare come true instead of a dream come true. The Keeper's Mentor, Wayn</span>
  <span id="freeText14722987122231394774" style="display:none"> A Review of Kingdom Keepers 3 by Ridley Pearson <br /> Being a Disney Host is glorious. You get to be a hologram guiding people around the Disney Parks. But Finn and his friends aren't just holograms that guide people around. At night, when they go to sleep, they wake up in Disney World as DHI's (holograms) and they fight evil to keep Disney safe. The "evil" is called the Overtakers, and they are trying to make Disney World a nightmare come true instead of a dream come true. The Keeper's Mentor, Wayne, is being kept hostage by the Overtakers but they don't know where. This book is called Kingdom Keepers 3 by: Ridley Pearson and it's a fantasy. Anyone who enjoys a mysterious adventure would really enjoy this. I like how this book makes you want to read on, how it's a mystery and also how they are on an adventure.<br /> In the whole Kingdom Keepers series, I've been wanting to read on, but in this one I wanted to continue the most. Kingdom Keepers 3 makes you want to keep going because when they walk around the park or go on a ride, something overwhelming happens. For an example, when the kids were riding Test Track, the car started going way faster then it's supposed to go out of nowhere. Also the seat belts got locked when Maleficent, the evil fairy, was chasing after their car. Another thing that kept me on the edge of my seat was when they were trying to get inside a building, but a gigantic fast snake was guarding it so they couldn't get inside.That part made me feel like I was actually being chased by a snake because of all the sound effects. Overall, this book kept me excited to keep reading. <br /> This book, like others in the series, was a mystery. It kept me interested about how they were solving a mystery of finding Wayne, their mentor. I was so anxious to find out where Wayne was throughout the book. For me when I was reading this book, I was relating it to the Scooby-Doo gang. Wayne left many challenging clues that they had to figure out. One of them was a big group of scrambled letters that they had to rearrange to find out where they had to look next. The clues were very interesting and hard to figure out. They even had to get help from their parents! I thought it was very cool how the Kingdom Keepers had to use the clues to find out where in the park or what ride the next clue would be at. Sometimes they even had to travel to a different park to find something out. <br /> One of the many fun touches that this book expressed was how they were on an adventure. Throughout the whole book, the Keepers were on an journey through the parks and rides. I enjoyed when they were in Epcot and statues came alive and started to fight them. When Jesters were chasing them around the different "countries", it was exciting. Did I also forget to mention that they pose as actors for "Fantasmic"? Things that look like just plain old robots during the day, go crazy with evilness at night.<br /> Overall this book is a great read. It will make you very excited to read on, for the whole book. There wasn't one part in this book where I was bored. I never wanted to put this book down. It will thrill teens who are obsessed with Disney World and characters. Once you read this book you will want to read it over and over again.<br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14722987122231394774" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_344464285" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/344464285" />
    <a title="Christine" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6414770-christine"><img alt="Christine" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1558856149p2/6414770.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/344464285?book_show_action=true">Jun 07, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christine" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christine" href="/user/show/6414770-christine">Christine</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Mystery, Suspense, Action, Fantasy, Logic, Children's, Science Fiction, Thriller fans</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Christine by: </span>
      Barnes and Noble
  </div>


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer344464285" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8555528348084022372">I really enjoyed this book. The next in the Kingdom Keepers series for me (which I seem to be zipping through quite quickly I must admit). I keep placing the next on hold and the next and the next (but currently I just left town, and my hold came in right as I was leaving, so I couldn't pick it up...) now the series is kind of on hold in terms of me finishing it (I was so close!). <br/><br/>This book is just a combination of genres...action, suspense, mystery, logic, children's, thriller, fantasy, sci-fi.</span>
  <span id="freeText8555528348084022372" style="display:none">I really enjoyed this book. The next in the Kingdom Keepers series for me (which I seem to be zipping through quite quickly I must admit). I keep placing the next on hold and the next and the next (but currently I just left town, and my hold came in right as I was leaving, so I couldn't pick it up...) now the series is kind of on hold in terms of me finishing it (I was so close!). <br /><br />This book is just a combination of genres...action, suspense, mystery, logic, children's, thriller, fantasy, sci-fi. The combination makes for one suspense-filled, riveting book.<br /><br />For once in the series, I found the title of this book fitting to the plot. The "shadow" part of the title hints to a key piece of the book as the Kingdom Keepers discover how to use the shadow, and it works to their advantage many times throughout the story.<br /><br />The plot focused on one single thing through the entire story, and it was a mad race for that through the whole story. This book was more like a puzzle, as the kids tried to figure out the clues Wayne had left them to save him. More of a mystery/detective novel. I liked it though, and it was really interesting and engaging. When I first got it I was like, "This is the thickest of the entire series so far!" But surprisingly enough, I read a lot of it in a short period of time. <br /><br />This series is really just a gem because it's one of the best action book/series I've picked up in a long time. It's really so interesting and enthralling that I recommend it to everyone. Just read the first book first (<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/953260.Disney_after_Dark__Kingdom_Keepers___1_" title="Disney after Dark (Kingdom Keepers, #1) by Ridley Pearson" rel="nofollow noopener">Disney after Dark</a>). And please read my review of it if you think it sounds cheesy <a href="https://www.goodreads.com" rel="nofollow noopener">http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/316989548</a>. It's really just an amazing, awesome series that I am so glad I found. And if you like Disney (not in a cheesy way, but true Disney), then you have to read this wonderful, marvelous, glorious series. Please! Read it! I love it!<br /><br /></span>

          </span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1541638129" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10933389422305507351">"Kingdom Keepers 3: Disney In Shadow follows the five teens, Finn, Philby, Willa, Charlene, and May beck as they search to find Wayne, their mentor and head Imagine-er who has mysteriously gone missing. Concerned Wayne has been abducted by the Over takers—Disney villains, who along with other Disney characters, take over the parks when the turnstiles stop spinning, and want desperately to steer the parks to a far darker place—the five kids pick up a major clue from a close friend, Jez, whose dre</span>
  <span id="freeText10933389422305507351" style="display:none">"Kingdom Keepers 3: Disney In Shadow follows the five teens, Finn, Philby, Willa, Charlene, and May beck as they search to find Wayne, their mentor and head Imagine-er who has mysteriously gone missing. Concerned Wayne has been abducted by the Over takers—Disney villains, who along with other Disney characters, take over the parks when the turnstiles stop spinning, and want desperately to steer the parks to a far darker place—the five kids pick up a major clue from a close friend, Jez, whose dreams (nightmares, really) often accurately predict the future. The very few clues from Jez’s dream lead the kids into Disney’s Hollywood Studios and Epcot--through imaginary worlds that become real, by imaginary kids who are real. Each clue seems tied to the last, and with the stakes growing ever higher, what starts out as a puzzle ends up as a fight for their lives. Through a transparent paper box, a quest for a sword, rides on Soaring' and Maelstrom, life-and-death encounters with giant snakes, and a devious Maleficent, the Kingdom Keepers not only begin to decipher deeper meanings to the clues, but discover new truths about themselves and their ever-growing friendships."<br /><br />The third of Ridley Pearson's Kingdom Keepers series takes its young protagonists to my favorite Walt Disney World park, EPCOT. <br /><br />Maleficent and Chernabog, captured and contained at the end of the second book, have escaped -- and taken the kids' Imagine friend, Wayne, with them. The book involves finding Wayne, with the help of his daughter, Wanda -- and takes the (now) six Disney Host Interactive models through a series of challenges and adventures.<br /><br />Part of what makes these books so much fun is that I've been on the rides and attractions they describe. Despite the fact that I'm much older than the intended audience for these tales, I'm thus able to put myself right into the action with the teenager characters.<br /><br />These books are a great deal of intelligent, escapist fun that is a safe read for the 10 and up set.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10933389422305507351" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_79807942" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/79807942" />
    <a title="Mitchel Broussard" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2536904-mitchel-broussard"><img alt="Mitchel Broussard" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577728446p2/2536904.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/79807942?book_show_action=true">Dec 03, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mitchel Broussard" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mitchel Broussard" href="/user/show/2536904-mitchel-broussard">Mitchel Broussard</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2536904-mitchel-broussard?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2536904-mitchel-broussard?shelf=ya-fiction">ya-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer79807942" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer292045087306096022">Probably the best of the series so far and a super quick read, despite its 500+ pages. The only thing i really didn't like was the conversation structure. It seemed when Mr. Pearson wanted to make a point he constructed a conversation to repeatedly state this point, and some lasted for almost 5 pages. It got a little annoying at times. I know the kids need to get to Epcot before midnight or their human selves will delve into comas, no need repeating it 7 times.<br/><br/>But otherwise, its the same great p</span>
  <span id="freeText292045087306096022" style="display:none">Probably the best of the series so far and a super quick read, despite its 500+ pages. The only thing i really didn't like was the conversation structure. It seemed when Mr. Pearson wanted to make a point he constructed a conversation to repeatedly state this point, and some lasted for almost 5 pages. It got a little annoying at times. I know the kids need to get to Epcot before midnight or their human selves will delve into comas, no need repeating it 7 times.<br /><br />But otherwise, its the same great premise: teens who had themselves digitized into holographic forms as Disney Park guides find that when they fall asleep they wake up as said holograms in the Parks. And they aren't alone, all the Disney characters come to life when everyone is gone, too (think <i> Toy Story. </i>) It still is a little foggy as to who knows about all the characters coming to life. I think some Disney workers know, but I'm not sure.<br /><br />Overall, this one was really good at presenting a mystery and series of clues and, for the most part, answering and solving it all. There are still a few hanging plot threads, and i know its a planned six series of books, so I have confidence that they'll be addressed soon.<br /><br />It really is a true improvement over the first sequel, <i> Disney at Dawn </i>, (which left me unsatisfied and more than a bit dissapointed.) My question is, how big is Mr. Pearson ready to make the books? He added nearly 250 pages with this one, any bigger and his targeted audience is gonna bolt. But i am completely fine with it, the writing and constant action make it a super quick read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="292045087306096022" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_425563869" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/425563869" />

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/425563869?book_show_action=true">Oct 01, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brenten Gilbert" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brenten Gilbert" href="/user/show/5776096-brenten-gilbert">Brenten Gilbert</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5776096-brenten-gilbert?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5776096-brenten-gilbert?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer425563869" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer132848287424258279">Rating: 3.5<br/><br/>The Kingdom Keepers return to action after yet another close call. They’re still on the lookout for their creator and guide, Wayne, who went missing after their second adventure. The group spends a lot of time exploring EPCOT and encounters opposition from the usual suspects, Maleficent and Chernabog, who plan to take control of the parks by leveraging a command center and holding park guests hostage. (I’m trying to be vague).<br/><br/>There are plenty of twists, turns, and close calls both in </span>
  <span id="freeText132848287424258279" style="display:none">Rating: 3.5<br /><br />The Kingdom Keepers return to action after yet another close call. They’re still on the lookout for their creator and guide, Wayne, who went missing after their second adventure. The group spends a lot of time exploring EPCOT and encounters opposition from the usual suspects, Maleficent and Chernabog, who plan to take control of the parks by leveraging a command center and holding park guests hostage. (I’m trying to be vague).<br /><br />There are plenty of twists, turns, and close calls both in the character’s real and DHI lives as they tackle their latest and greatest set of challenges. They find new ways to face their enemies (who include a giant python - as seen on the cover) and they work together to make the most of their talents. It did seem like a memo had been sent down from management for Pearson to emphasize the advantage of teamwork over individualism, however, as several times throughout the book, the point was painstakingly underlined and highlighted. <br /><br />Overall though, the books series continues well, with a compelling story line and near non-stop action. I’ve already begun book four as I bounce back and forth between Kingdom Keepers and Starcatchers. So much Disney, I might explode. <br /><br />-from TRudATmusic[dot]com[slash]raw</span>
  <a data-text-id="132848287424258279" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_674010830" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/674010830" />
    <a title="MS Meagher" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10212843-ms-meagher"><img alt="MS Meagher" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1341745678p2/10212843.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/674010830?book_show_action=true">Jul 22, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="MS Meagher" class="user" itemprop="url" name="MS Meagher" href="/user/show/10212843-ms-meagher">MS Meagher</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10212843-ms-meagher?shelf=a-unshelved">a-unshelved</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer674010830" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9332188271065028224">Reading this book with my three children aged 9, 12 and 15. We read together a lot, and they've become quite selective about book choice. The general consensus is these books are good, exciting and worth continuing with, but you have to overlook the enormous plot holes, the huge amount of time given in each book to regurgitating the events of the past, which usually includes adding new significant details not mentioned previously, and the habit of revising past writing to try to deal with obviou</span>
  <span id="freeText9332188271065028224" style="display:none">Reading this book with my three children aged 9, 12 and 15. We read together a lot, and they've become quite selective about book choice. The general consensus is these books are good, exciting and worth continuing with, but you have to overlook the enormous plot holes, the huge amount of time given in each book to regurgitating the events of the past, which usually includes adding new significant details not mentioned previously, and the habit of revising past writing to try to deal with obvious plot holes or allow for new twists in the story. As an adult, I find them quite annoying, and not particularly well written (I get the feeling he was writing to a deadline which didn't suit him, and there are some editing issues) and even the 9 year old sees glaring errors, but the suspense makes up for it, and we've bought the rest of the series so these books do have something going for them and are worth a try. You just have to take them with a very large pinch of salt.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9332188271065028224" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
