<span id="freeTextContainer6849133386817270067">3.5 stars. I liked this book okay. The only reason I rated it that low was because I felt it was way longer than it needed to be. I think the book could have covered everything in 100 pages less. And I STILL don't quite understand what's going on. I feel like the author is holding back information. After 1,000+ pages, I would like to know where the series is going to go. <br/>And the relationships he has going on are so confusing. And I get that relationships are confusing at this age, but it seems t</span>
  <span id="freeText6849133386817270067" style="display:none">3.5 stars. I liked this book okay. The only reason I rated it that low was because I felt it was way longer than it needed to be. I think the book could have covered everything in 100 pages less. And I STILL don't quite understand what's going on. I feel like the author is holding back information. After 1,000+ pages, I would like to know where the series is going to go. <br />And the relationships he has going on are so confusing. And I get that relationships are confusing at this age, but it seems the author doesn't know what he wants to do with them yet! One of them was finally cleared up in the last 2 pages, but that's the only one so far. <br />I'd recommend this book for kids 11-14 I think. <br />So, I'll keep reading the series, but I'm going to take as break from it for now. I bought 6 books this last weekend and I'm really excited about all of them! So I'm going to read some of those for now, then eventually come back for this. :)</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1441295083" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15031648079753617832">This book ruined the kingdom keepers series for me, it was so boring and predictable that I did not enjoy reading it at all. The charaters are the typical high school kids who each have one thing in common, and that is they go on adventures to disneyworld when they start sleeping. The books each start out the same way by recapping the last. I think that the reader should know what happend in the last kne before they read a new book thats later in the series. Another weekness is that the charater</span>
  <span id="freeText15031648079753617832" style="display:none">This book ruined the kingdom keepers series for me, it was so boring and predictable that I did not enjoy reading it at all. The charaters are the typical high school kids who each have one thing in common, and that is they go on adventures to disneyworld when they start sleeping. The books each start out the same way by recapping the last. I think that the reader should know what happend in the last kne before they read a new book thats later in the series. Another weekness is that the charaters do not have any personality that distinct themselvs from the others. They all act almost exactly the same and all have very similar ideas. I will not continue to read this series as it is not appealing to me anymore and that there are much better books/novels to read (ex.unbroken). I think that the common audience would not enjoy this book because there is no "real" variation to this book and the last book. </span>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/419327840?book_show_action=true">Sep 21, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sharon" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sharon" href="/user/show/1757121-sharon">Sharon</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer419327840" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9623416336191923682">The third of Ridley Pearson's Kingdom Keepers series takes its young protagonists to my favorite Walt Disney World park, EPCOT. <br/><br/>Maleficent and Chernabog, captured and contained at the end of the second book, have escaped -- and taken the kids' Imagineer friend, Wayne, with them. The book involves finding Wayne, with the help of his daughter, Wanda -- and takes the (now) six Disney Host Interactive models through a series of challenges and adventures.<br/><br/>Part of what makes these books so much fun is </span>
  <span id="freeText9623416336191923682" style="display:none">The third of Ridley Pearson's Kingdom Keepers series takes its young protagonists to my favorite Walt Disney World park, EPCOT. <br /><br />Maleficent and Chernabog, captured and contained at the end of the second book, have escaped -- and taken the kids' Imagineer friend, Wayne, with them. The book involves finding Wayne, with the help of his daughter, Wanda -- and takes the (now) six Disney Host Interactive models through a series of challenges and adventures.<br /><br />Part of what makes these books so much fun is that I've been on the rides and attractions they describe. Despite the fact that I'm much older than the intended audience for these tales, I'm thus able to put myself right into the action with the teenaged characters.<br /><br />These books are a great deal of intelligent, escapist fun that is a safe read for the 10 and up set.</span>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('JhJlk33/40KbHo1ZavsPxDAdSeZ/w99mQpWkCqTIoEgt5VaXlpqRvP/zRyoi2Rc+CzXOQEq9MuHdQhv3G6WIDw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {

  <span id="freeText13983238530863019116" style="display:none">Ridley Pearson is the author of more than fifty novels, including the <em>New York Times</em> bestseller <em>Killer Weekend</em>; the Lou Boldt crime series; and many books for young readers, including the award-winning children's novels <em>Peter and the Starcatchers</em>, <em>Peter and the Shadow Thieves</em>, and <em>Peter and the Secret of Rundoon</em>, which he cowrote with Dave Barry. Pearson lives with his wife and two daughters, dividing their time between Missouri and Idaho.<br /><br />Also writes Chris Klick mysteries as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/260141.Wendell_McCall" rel="nofollow noopener">Wendell McCall</a>.</span>
